<div id="review_833286705" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/833286705" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11410830-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344005470p2/11410830.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/833286705?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/11410830-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11410830-paul?shelf=crime-thrillers">crime-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer833286705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13539746244685163401">Silent but deadly<br/><br/>The Silent Wife by A.S.A. Harrison was her debut novel and unfortunately her last as she died in 2013 in which she has left an incredible psychological thriller. This is no ordinary thriller either where we see the perpetrator and the detectives for them. This is far darker, far deeper inside the mind and is so engrossing it is tempting to rush through the book. I do not know how Harrison has done it but she has reached inside the mind to those dark deep well hidden depths we al</span>
  <span id="freeText13539746244685163401" style="display:none">Silent but deadly<br /><br />The Silent Wife by A.S.A. Harrison was her debut novel and unfortunately her last as she died in 2013 in which she has left an incredible psychological thriller. This is no ordinary thriller either where we see the perpetrator and the detectives for them. This is far darker, far deeper inside the mind and is so engrossing it is tempting to rush through the book. I do not know how Harrison has done it but she has reached inside the mind to those dark deep well hidden depths we all have and brings it all out for the reader.<br /><br />This story is that Jodi Brett who has lived with Todd Gilbert for over twenty years, she is a psychologist and her common law husband is a property developer, knows all about his faults and has accepted them. She understands that he is a lothario as long as he does not bring it to her doorstep over the years he has had numerous affairs and always come home. She lives the denial as if in a parallel universe but always settle the score with him.<br /><br />We see Todd fall in lust with a younger lover, a student whom he gets pregnant and she becomes more demanding wanting changes in his life. He leaves Jodi and starts eviction proceedings against her from the place she calls home and cuts off her money. Really he is a lover not a fighter and Natasha his young love has to push him all the way.<br /><br />What makes this book so brilliant as a thriller is that we see it through the eyes of Jodi and Todd in alternating voices we see how they live and feel to them attempting to move on. We have the voice of killer and victim which brings quite a lot of sympathy for Jodi as the wronged woman. There are plenty of twists and turns and we are with Jodi are killer all the way through, and that is no spoiler as it tells you on the cover! How things actually work out is something well worth reading, very enjoyable and consuming at the same time dark and treacherous which ticks all the thriller boxes. I cannot recommend The Silent Wife highly enough.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13539746244685163401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17330705423286553336">**Received from Goodreads first reads giveaway.<br/><br/>This was a great psychological book. It is the story of a 20 year common law marriage (and both parties) falling apart. We witness the disintegration of their relationship through both Jodi and Todd's point of view. We see how they rationalize, excuse, cope and justify their behavior. Todd is a habitual cheater and Jodi is aware but never confronts him on it but always lets him know that she will be there for him waiting with elegant meals and pleas</span>
  <span id="freeText17330705423286553336" style="display:none">**Received from Goodreads first reads giveaway.<br /><br />This was a great psychological book. It is the story of a 20 year common law marriage (and both parties) falling apart. We witness the disintegration of their relationship through both Jodi and Todd's point of view. We see how they rationalize, excuse, cope and justify their behavior. Todd is a habitual cheater and Jodi is aware but never confronts him on it but always lets him know that she will be there for him waiting with elegant meals and pleasant conversation. Denial is what holds them together. Both seem to be fine with this arrangement until he gets the daughter of his best friend pregnant. This is where the unraveling really begins.<br /><br />This book was great. Even though I have mentioned the plot there is more much more. Subtle nuances, subtleties that really make this book work, some twists, turns and well....read it for yourself. I highly recommend this book.</span>

From page 1 we know she ends up killing his cheating ass, but we don't know how or when. There is not much action or dialogue, just a very suspenseful and methodical revealing of their individual personalities and psyches. There is more here than meets the eye. Great book.</span>

  <span id="freeText15352602921708894422" style="display:none">3.5 stars !<br /><br />This was a taut psychological thriller that was well-researched and with a slow unfolding of the dynamics of two very narcissistic individuals....the wife (a psychotherapist with obsessive tendencies) and the husband (immature businessman) and the slow death of their marriage that was fragile and empty to begin with.<br /><br />Both characters were quite unlikable but they were infused with a complexity that compelled you to read forward and see what would happen next. I also liked the Adlerian aspects of this book and the delving into the character's psyches.<br /><br />This book was MUCH BETTER than GONE GIRL but like Gone Girl there were some inconsistencies that at times verged on the ridiculous. However, in this book it was much more forgivable as the dark unfolding was fascinating, morbid and really quite shocking.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10072946543986893489"><br/>Jodi Bret and Todd Gilbert - who have been together for twenty years - live in a posh Chicago condominium and enjoy the good things in life: a lovely home; expensive cars; fine dining; evening walks along the lake; etc. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559851788i/27628822.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Jodi is a trained psychotherapist and maintains an office in the condo. She sees a couple of patients a day, and spends the rest of her time working out, reading, walking the couple's dog Freud, seeing friends, shopping, cooking gourmet meals, etc. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559851788i/27628821._SY540_.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Todd is a successful developer </span>
  <span id="freeText10072946543986893489" style="display:none"><br>Jodi Bret and Todd Gilbert - who have been together for twenty years - live in a posh Chicago condominium and enjoy the good things in life: a lovely home; expensive cars; fine dining; evening walks along the lake; etc. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559851788i/27628822.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jodi is a trained psychotherapist and maintains an office in the condo. She sees a couple of patients a day, and spends the rest of her time working out, reading, walking the couple's dog Freud, seeing friends, shopping, cooking gourmet meals, etc. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559851788i/27628821._SY540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Todd is a successful developer who's currently experiencing a money crunch because of a pricey building renovation. Todd likes to ogle women, show off his expensive possessions, and spend time with Jodi - who coddles and indulges him.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559851788i/27628825.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The couple's lives are humming along smoothly when Todd mentions that he'll be going on a fishing trip next weekend, with some fellows from the office. Jodi immediately sniffs out the lie, and it's one lie too many.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559851788i/27628823.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jodi knows that Todd is a serial womanizer, and Todd is aware that she knows. However, Todd's behavior has NEVER been acknowledged between them. Thus the evenings when Todd is 'working late' or 'having a drink with the boys' have passed without reproach, though Jodi does small vindictive things for revenge. Todd has never gone away for an entire weekend, though, and this seems to spell trouble.<br><br>Indeed it spells trouble.....BIG trouble. Todd has been seeing a sexy college coed named Natasha, who happens to be the daughter of his best friend Dean. Worse yet, Natasha is pregnant and expects Todd to marry her. Natasha and Todd's upcoming weekend getaway, planned by the coed, is to be a romantic interlude and an opportunity to discuss their (really her) plans. Number one on Natasha's list is for Todd to tell Jodi what's going on and move out.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559851788i/27628824.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Todd doesn't have the nerve to inform Jodi, but she finds out anyway - from Dean, who's furious about Todd knocking up his daughter. Even afterwards, when Todd knows that Jodi's been told, neither of them brings up the subject. In fact things at home go on much as before.....for a while. (Can you imagine a more fraught state of affairs?)<br><br>Todd knows he has to cut the cord at some point, and - once lawyers get involved - Jodi discovers that she's entitled to nothing because she and Todd were never married. Things eventually take a dark turn, which is foreshadowed at the beginning of the book.<br><br>The story alternates back and forth between Jodi's perspective and Todd's perspective, and we learn that they both come from dysfunctional families. In Jodi's chapters we read about her parents and two brothers. We also see flashbacks to Jodi's psychotherapy sessions, which took place during graduate school. Jody's psychoanalysis reveals some hard truths, and may be meant to explain her passive-aggressive behavior - but it's a stretch (IMO). <br><br>For his part, Todd is unable to hold his own against Natasha, whose assertive personality is the diametric opposite of Jodi's. Natasha is continually pushing Todd in directions he'd rather not go and is planning a huge wedding he can't afford right now. Todd's angst about all this has predictable results.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559851788i/27628820._SX540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I listened to the audio version of this book, which was a mistake. The female narrator - who voices Jodi's chapters - speaks exceptionally slowly, probably to depict Jodi's shock at the crisis in her life. This makes the story, which is already slow, feel moribund. The male narrator - who voice's Todd's sections - is a bit better....but the tale still meanders along.<br><br>I found the story interesting from the perspective of two damaged people in a seriously neurotic relationship. A couple going on like this for twenty years seems incomprehensible to me. I'm especially bewildered by Jodi, who (it would seem) could do much better than a lying cheat. <br><br>I didn't particularly like the book, but readers interested in psychology and flawed relationships might be interested.<br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot....</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10072946543986893489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11595647378533532243">I really shouldn't read blurbs, because they raise expectations too high. Calling this akin to <i>Gone Girl</i> makes some sense: we have dual points-of-view, we have a husband and wife in a "meh" marriage with problems, and there's a murder (the wife, Jodi, actually says that she never thought she'd be a killer somewhere in the early stages of the book). Are the narrators unreliable? No idea. I read 30% (per my Kindle's reckoning) and gave up.<br/><br/>Where this differed from <i>Gone Girl</i> for me was that I didn't</span>
  <span id="freeText11595647378533532243" style="display:none">I really shouldn't read blurbs, because they raise expectations too high. Calling this akin to <i>Gone Girl</i> makes some sense: we have dual points-of-view, we have a husband and wife in a "meh" marriage with problems, and there's a murder (the wife, Jodi, actually says that she never thought she'd be a killer somewhere in the early stages of the book). Are the narrators unreliable? No idea. I read 30% (per my Kindle's reckoning) and gave up.<br /><br />Where this differed from <i>Gone Girl</i> for me was that I didn't care about the situation or Jodi and Todd. While in GG I didn't like them, the plot was interesting enough to bring me along. Plus, not liking them was part of the author's intent. That may have been the case here, but the way in which we're introduced to what happened is so slow, giving me two people I really didn't want to read about with no "why you should read further" in that first 30%. <br /><br />ARC provided by publisher.</span>

<div id="review_779549497" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/779549497" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/779549497?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=better-than-i-expected">better-than-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=multi-povs">multi-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer779549497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12211303102391286142">Quick review for not such a quick read, but still a captivating one. I'll admit I picked up A.S.A. Harrison's "The Silent Wife" because it was rec'd to me by my library for follow-up reads to Gillian Flynn's "Gone Girl". I'm not going to evoke any other comparisons to the latter work other than that mention, because this book is a whole different ballgame, but I can see why the comparison comes about.<br/><br/>"The Silent Wife" is one of those books that is definitely hit and miss. The characters are flaw</span>
  <span id="freeText12211303102391286142" style="display:none">Quick review for not such a quick read, but still a captivating one. I'll admit I picked up A.S.A. Harrison's "The Silent Wife" because it was rec'd to me by my library for follow-up reads to Gillian Flynn's "Gone Girl". I'm not going to evoke any other comparisons to the latter work other than that mention, because this book is a whole different ballgame, but I can see why the comparison comes about.<br /><br />"The Silent Wife" is one of those books that is definitely hit and miss. The characters are flawed and unlikable, the style of the prose is literary and has this slow unfurling, which is unlike the purported "thriller" that it's advertised as. I will definitely say that it's a solid mystery and supsenseful, but I wouldn't consider it a pulse-pounding thriller because it's about as quiet in its methodical unveiling as its title. "The Silent Wife" is symbolic, because in the silence of the woman who is the title's namesake, there's a whole lot of baggage to be had, secrets under the surface, and assumptions that you think would be teetering on the precipice of being unveiled, but not quite there. It's this game of whether or not you think the rug will be pulled out from under you, and it may or may not depending on the circumstance.<br /><br />It was difficult for me to get into, what with the trading between two perspectives - man and woman - in a third person narrative where the two are in a slowly deteriorating marriage, and both are in a state of denial about such a state as well as their own shortcomings. Jodi knows her husband is a serial cheater, but chooses to live in denial about it, and there's this slow festering of dissent and anger that bubbles up inside her waiting to burst. Then comes the moment where it's one too many misgivings, and all hell breaks loose. Todd is a serial cheater who also lives in denial - on one hand he's unwilling to leave Jodi after their partnership of 20 years, but you could argue that he's seeking to use her and then lose her the first chance he gets. When a bombshell about one of his "flings" comes to light, then things are solidified towards the demise of his union with a Jodi.<br /><br />This book is deliciously dark and well-plotted, which is one of the reasons why I followed it and found it well despite its problematic backdrops. Granted, I didn't like any of the characters. Todd is a jerk and his opinion and attention changes at the drop of a hat when it comes to serving his own interests and thinking self-indulgently. He thinks with his netherregions and revelations about his character reveal even more about his selfishness than anything else. Jodi isn't much better, because in her silence and denial - despite her being a mental health professional, she's cold and calculating and she's on pins and needles as far as her mental state deterioration is concerned. But in a way, I understood the way Jodi thought and felt based on how the narrative presented her perspective and rationale to me. Granted, it made me want to rage, but I could follow her perspective through the story and it kept me on edge the entire time. Will she, or won't she? Did she, or did she not? I guessed what the ending was a little while before it came (there is a twist here), but it still surprised me all the same - for coincidence and for how the end came about by context. I did wish that the narrative pacing was more even for the reveal and building up to that point, but I understood what the author was trying to do in that steady build toward Jodi's and Todd's respective fates (notice I'm trying to tap dance around events because I don't want to spoil it).<br /><br />In the end, it's a read that was worth the journey and I appreciated it - for plotting, for the development, and for the respective reveal leaving my head turning even after the last few minutes of the audio. The audiobook was decent, though I think the narration from the female perspective (read by Karen White) was a little on the monotonous side. I think that was intentional based on the kind of character that Jodi was, but in the beginning of the narrative, I felt the weight of it was a bit odd for matching (it improved as certain events came to pass and I learned a bit more about the character). Todd's narrator (Donald Corren) was pitch perfect throughout. I'd recommend trying this one, though I'm aware that there may be many who will either love it or hate it for the character actions and its slow, steady build, but the calculating weight and dark tone of this story did impress me, as well as its subsequent development and reveal.<br /><br />Overall score: 4/5 stars </span>
  <a data-text-id="12211303102391286142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_843455602" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/843455602" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/843455602?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer843455602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11165042782204676203">3.5 Stars<br/><br/>"She hasn't said a word but she has him on the run." <br/><br/>I love silence. There's a certain amount of power in it. I wish that I had the ability to say everything by saying nothing, but that is not one of my talents. I wish that my love of silence could be stronger than my love of being fucking <i>right</i>, but alas, I'm opinionated, and I have no problem sharing my opinions. I have no problem standing up for myself and what I think is right.<br/><br/>Unlike Jodi, our main character. She absorbs. All of the</span>
  <span id="freeText11165042782204676203" style="display:none">3.5 Stars<br /><br />"She hasn't said a word but she has him on the run." <br /><br />I love silence. There's a certain amount of power in it. I wish that I had the ability to say everything by saying nothing, but that is not one of my talents. I wish that my love of silence could be stronger than my love of being fucking <i>right</i>, but alas, I'm opinionated, and I have no problem sharing my opinions. I have no problem standing up for myself and what I think is right.<br /><br />Unlike Jodi, our main character. She absorbs. All of the cruel, degrading, and humiliating ways that a cheating significant other can cause pain, and she takes them all in silently, rationally, and then lets them go, because to her, keeping up appearances and order are more important than being strong enough to refuse to do so. <br /><br />He, Todd, isn't even aware of this. He cheats because he thinks it is natural, and because he has no reason NOT to cheat. His dinner is cooked, his home is beautiful, Jodi is accommodating and forgiving and loving. And predictable and boring. But comfortable. But constraining. Familiar, but unexciting... You get the idea. She's the status quo, and he's in the middle of a midlife crisis. <br /><br />And thus, the Pretty Young Thing, the wrench, finds its way into the works and all the gears that have been smoothly fitting together and working just fine for 20 years or so come to a grinding halt. <br /><br />All of this makes for an interesting premise. What exactly pushes this woman, this calm, rational, optimistic, believer in soul-mates who has ignored 20 years of blatant cheating, to the point of murder? <br /><br />I often don't know how I really feel about a book until I'm hashing out my thoughts in a review. This is definitely one of those books, because while I think it was effective at showing just how one gets pushed to the point of no return, I had some definite issues with it at the same time. Not least of which was the narrative voice. This book is told in alternating 3rd person limited perspectives (His and Hers viewpoints), but it's in present tense. Which I dislike. In this case, from the very beginning, it felt more like a 3rd party was relating each of the sides of the story than that we were actually seeing things from Jodi's and Todd's perspectives. There were little asides, little clarifications, tiny moments which took me out of the story and made me wonder who is actually relating all of this to me. The present tense and generally commiserative tone actually created distance for me, and made me feel like I was being shepherded or led to certain conclusions, being manipulated by someone I wasn't even aware was a player in the story. <br /><br />But, if I ignore that, I find a story that is surprisingly perceptive and understandable. I can see how a relationship could get to that point of stasis and stagnation and obliviousness. She thinking that providing structure and predictable domesticity and acceptance of his flaws was love, and he failing to recognize her forms of love, and feeling that the lack of excitement or challenge is stifling, but still needing and appreciating the unquestioning home-base she offered. <br /><br />I will say that there was one detail that I initially thought was superfluous though, which was the memory resurrected by the dream Jodi recounted to Gerard. I didn't understand the relevance of adding this bit into the story until well after I'd finished and thought about it for a while. Only after giving it time to settle in my mind did I realize that that memory is what shaped her into the woman she is when we meet her - the one who absorbs it all and then puts it aside, and focuses on others, and does it all in silence. It makes sense why she makes the choices she's made, regarding marriage and children and her family and how she wants to live unattached - at least on paper. I think, had she shared that memory with Todd, that they might've understood each other a little better. But she isn't the sharing type... she's the absorbing type, and Todd takes her constancy for granted. <br /><br />He's a "grass is always greener in someone else's pasture" kind of guy. I have to admit that I felt kind of bad for him at times, because his new grass may be young and green and pretty to look at, but if you rub it the wrong way, it's got sharp edges. But by then he'd made his bed and had to lie in it, silently regretting leaving the soft, comfy grass he'd been used to for so long. As they say, you don't know what you got 'til it's gone.<br /><br />This is a slow build of a story, even though it is a quick read. I didn't find myself racing through it because the tension was palpable and I just had to know what happens next, but I did find it compelling and intriguing, and I wanted to know where it would go next. This didn't have the urgency and the chaos and edge-of-your-seat drama of Gone Girl, but for someone intrigued by the "when relationships go wrong" breakdown, this is an interesting derailing to watch. <br /><br />I found myself surprisingly conflicted toward the end of the book though. We know all along that she's going to commit murder - we learn that on page two. How she gets there and how she does it and what happens after are the questions we continue reading to find out. I wasn't a huge Jodi supporter throughout the story (I think she made her own bed of poorly-communicated expectations and failures to compromise, combined with an appalling willingness to accept his indiscretions), but I could sympathize with her to a point, and understood what drove her to do what she did. I even found myself rooting for her to get away with it... until the very end, which just felt too much like deus ex machina for my liking. <br /><br />Anyway, this was a pretty good story, and it definitely had its ups and downs, but I don't think it really compares with Gone Girl. That story was a rollercoaster ride, filled with flips and twists and stomach-in-your-throat plummeting drops. This one was more like a ride through a haunted house in an amusement park. It's a slower pace through a dark and dank area, and you know there's something nasty waiting around the corner, but it's never quite as ugly as you thought it would be. Still, you'd go again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11165042782204676203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sEa2LWlMwK9titqNnPFNUY5LtAc+Kr1GTXO8BFADx9oe5MokQp0Lu1tVy90dtwAmMBJAmCOxiOYXAAcy25MfAg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4672071.A_S_A_Harrison">About A.S.A. Harrison</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4672071.A_S_A_Harrison"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1395291484p3/4672071.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4672071.A_S_A_Harrison">A.S.A. Harrison
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
399
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10834948819971741956">A. S. A (Susan) Harrison’s previous books include Orgasms (Coach House Press, 1974), Revelations, with Margaret Dragu (Nightwood Editions, 1987), and Zodicat Speaks (Viking Penguin, 1996). <i>The Silent Wife</i> is her debut novel and she was at work on a new psychological thriller when she died in 2013, aged 65. Harrison was married to the visual artist John Massey and lived in Toronto.</span>

</div>
</div>
